{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","title":"How to Make a Day of the Dead Mask","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Day of the Dead is a Mexican holiday honoring lost loved ones that's celebrated around the same time as Halloween. Making a Day of the Dead mask is a great way to teach kids about the holiday while also passing a fun afternoon making crafts. The easiest solution, especially if you’re doing this with young children or as a classroom activity, is to print out skull templates and make paper masks. Just cut them out and decorate them however you’d like! If you're creating a costume, grab a plain white plastic mask from a craft store and decorate it with traditional Day of the Dead designs. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Creating a Simple Paper Mask\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Creating-a-Simple-Paper-Mask\">Creating a Simple Paper Mask</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Search for a Day of the Dead skull shape template online. You can find a lot of cool Day of the Dead mask templates online. If you have small children or are planning this as a classroom activity, this is a great option. Run a search for “Day of the Dead mask template” or “calavera template” and browse through the available options.<br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make a Day of the Dead Mask Step 1 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0f/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid2104507-v4-728px-Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re having trouble finding templates, check out the 4 printable options here: <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://drive.google.com/file/d/0B95QypGcCj4ZT2x5NnBNb2VUd00/edit\">https://drive.google.com/file/d/0B95QypGcCj4ZT2x5NnBNb2VUd00/edit</a></li> \n    <li>You can find another template option here: <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"https://www.triedandtrueblog.com/triedandtrue/wp-content/uploads/2012/10/diadelosmuertos_printable_heart1.pdf\">https://www.triedandtrueblog.com/triedandtrue/wp-content/uploads/2012/10/diadelosmuertos_printable_heart1.pdf</a></li> \n    <li>You can also check your local craft store for wooden skull masks or Day of the Dead skull coloring pages.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Print out the template on regular printer paper or cardstock. Regular white printer paper will work just fine for this, but if you want something sturdier, use construction paper or cardstock for your mask. You don’t need any colored ink for this—black ink works perfectly and creates an authentic look.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make a Day of the Dead Mask Step 2 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/97/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid2104507-v4-728px-Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Don’t worry—you'll be decorating the mask later, so you can make it as colorful as you like at that point.</li> \n    <li>Many templates have designs on the skull already, which makes it super easy to create an authentic-looking mask. You can choose a blank skull template and draw in your own designs if you prefer, though.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cut around the perimeter of the skull to create the base of the mask. Printable templates have easy-to-follow lines that you or your child can easily cut out. Use a pair of sharp scissors to cut out the skull template and toss the excess paper in the trash.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Cut out the eye holes if you want a mask you can see through. You don’t have to do this, but it can make the masks more fun and interactive.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Draw in traditional Day of the Dead designs with a Sharpie, if desired. The easiest templates already have authentic details and designs included on the skull face. If you printed out a blank skull template, use a permanent black marker to draw on flowers, hearts, animals, curlicue shapes, and other traditional Day of the Dead designs.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>It can help to look at traditional designs online and mimic them if you aren’t sure what to draw on your skull.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use markers or crayons to color in the designs any way you’d like. Day of the Dead skulls are traditionally quite colorful, so feel free to use any colors that you’d like to fill in the designs. Bright colors like orange, yellow, and aqua are common, but you can really go with any color palette you want. Encourage the kids to get creative!<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Add fun accents like glitter, sequins, or stick-on rhinestones, if desired. Feel free to customize your mask any way you’d like. Glitter glue is an easy, no-mess way to add some sparkle. Stick-on rhinestones and other cool stickers are great options. Gluing felt designs onto the face or a plastic flower at the temple can also look really cool.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Use hot glue to attach felt, sequins, or plastic flowers securely to the mask. If you’re working with small children, you might want to handle this part yourself.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Glue the paper mask to the top of a wooden popsicle stick. Add a dab of hot glue to the end of a wooden popsicle stick or craft stick. Then, press the chin area of the mask carefully onto the glue to attach the wooden stick. Give the glue a few minutes to dry and hold up your Day of the Dead mask to your face.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>School glue or super glue will also work.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Talk about the significance of the holiday as you work with the kids. Day of the Dead is a Mexican celebration that happens on the first 2 days of November. It's believed that the passageway between the real world and the spirit world is open during this time so deceased loved ones can visit their families. Families prepare by creating altars, decorating graves, and cooking traditional foods.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make a Day of the Dead Mask Step 8 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/28/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-8-Version-2.jpg/aid2104507-v4-728px-Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Festivities are joyful and often include flowers, music, candles, singing, and dancing.</li> \n    <li>Day of the Dead has been celebrated for centuries and it's roots stretch back to the time of the Aztecs.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Making a Strap-On Costume Mask\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Making-a-Strap-On-Costume-Mask\">Making a Strap-On Costume Mask</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Cover your work surface with cardboard or plastic to protect it. Crafting can get messy! Place a large piece of cardboard on your work surface or tape down a garbage bag so you don't damage the surface.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-9-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make a Day of the Dead Mask Step 9 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/44/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-9-Version-2.jpg/aid2104507-v4-728px-Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-9-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Be sure to work on a flat, stable surface with plenty of room to spread out your craft supplies.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Cut a plastic craft mask around the edges to create a skull shape. Plain white craft masks are usually rounded, but you can use scissors to alter the shape. Cut into the mask about at one of the skull's temples to create a slight indention. Then, cut around the top of the skull to the other temple and cut another indention. Do the same thing under the cheekbones on each side of the face to for an authentic skull shape.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can find plain white craft masks made of plastic or cardboard at most craft stores. Be sure to get a mask that has an elastic strap so you can wear your mask once it’s done.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Sketch lines around the eyes, nose, and mouth to create a skull face. Use a pencil to lightly sketch in large teeth around the mouth area. Then, change the eyes to be perfectly round circles. Lightly draw an upside-down heart over the nose area so your mask will look like a skull with a skeleton face.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Draw your favorite Day of the Dead designs on other areas of the skull. Traditional designs include flowers, hearts, curlicues, paisley patterns, and so on. You can place your designs anywhere you'd like. Drawing flower petals around the eyes is a traditional look, but you can be as creative as you want.<br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you need inspiration or want to see traditional designs, type “Day of the Dead” mask into your search engine and check out the image results that pop up.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Fill in the eye and nose shapes with black paint or permanent marker. If you’re using black craft paint, use a paintbrush to fill in the eye circles and upside-down heart nose completely. A black Sharpie will create the same effect, so use whatever tools you feel the most comfortable with or have handy.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you'd like, draw or paint a black line between the upper and lower teeth and extend the line to the hollow areas under each cheekbone. Then, fill in the small hollow on each side to create a skeleton mouth.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use colorful paint or permanent markers to fill in your sketched designs. Day of the Dead masks are traditionally very bright, so feel free to use any color palette that you like. Yellow, blue, red, orange, and green are all great options for your mask.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Give paint an hour or so to dry before moving on to the next step. If you used permanent marker, this should only take a few minutes.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Outline the designs with black 3D paint or a black Sharpie. Make sure paint is totally dry before you do this! Then, outline all of your designs in black for a traditional look. Using a black permanent marker is an easy option, but you can also create cool texture with squeeze tubes of 3D paint.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can buy 3D paint in squeeze tubes from any craft store.</li> \n    <li>Try accenting the black outlines with gold or silver for an even cooler look!</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Hot glue small craft gems to the skull, if desired. Adding small gems to some of the empty spaces on the skull can take your mask to the next level. Use hot glue to attach the gems or buy the stick-on variety and press them on wherever you like.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-16.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make a Day of the Dead Mask Step 16.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/aa/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-16.jpg/aid2104507-v4-728px-Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-16.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>To make your design super durable, you may want to add hot glue to the stick-on variety, as well.</li> \n    <li>You can buy small craft gems at any craft store or order them online.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Let the mask dry overnight before you wear it. Put the mask somewhere out of the way and let the glue and paint set. At minimum, allow 5-6 hours for this. If possible, let everything set overnight so your mask will be extra durable.<sup id=\"_ref-17\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 17\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask#_note-17\">[17]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-17.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make a Day of the Dead Mask Step 17.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/20/Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-17.jpg/aid2104507-v4-728px-Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask-Step-17.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>When you're ready to wear your mask, hold it in front of your face and stretch the elastic band over your head to keep it in place.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Video\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Video\">Video</span></h2> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Feel free to decorate your mask in any way that you’d like. This project is really customizable and fun.</li> \n  <li>Cut out the eye holes if you want to be able to see through the mask.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Be careful with hot glue! If you’re working with young children, it’s best to handle the hot glue yourself.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Things You’ll Need\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Things-You’ll-Need\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Things-You.E2.80.99ll-Need\">Things You’ll Need</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Creating a Simple Paper Mask\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Creating-a-Simple-Paper-Mask_2\">Creating a Simple Paper Mask</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>Printer paper or construction paper</li> \n  <li>Scissors</li> \n  <li>Black Sharpie (optional)</li> \n  <li>Markers or crayons</li> \n  <li>Glitter glue (optional)</li> \n  <li>Stick-on rhinestones (optional)</li> \n  <li>Sequins (optional)</li> \n  <li>Puffy paint (optional)</li> \n  <li>1 wooden popsicle stick per mask</li> \n  <li>Hot glue or school glue</li>\n </ul> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Making a Strap-On Costume Mask\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Making-a-Strap-On-Costume-Mask_2\">Making a Strap-On Costume Mask</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>Cardboard or plastic garbage bags</li> \n  <li>Plain white craft mask (plastic or cardboard)</li> \n  <li>Scissors</li> \n  <li>Pencil</li> \n  <li>Craft paint or permanent markers</li> \n  <li>3D paint (optional)</li> \n  <li>Small craft gems (optional)</li> \n  <li>Hot glue (optional)</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-a-Day-of-the-Dead-Mask&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10\" title=\"Edit section: References\">Edit</a><span reatedDate":1604381483030},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","title":"How to Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\"><p>This wikiHow teaches you how to join a Zoom conference call or meeting you've been invited to, using a computer. You can join a Zoom meeting with your internet browser on PC, Mac or Linux.\n</p>\n<h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac&#38;action=edit&#38;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2>\n<h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac&#38;action=edit&#38;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Joining With an Email Invite\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Joining-With-an-Email-Invite\">Joining With an Email Invite</span></h3>\n<ol><li>Open the Zoom meeting invitation in your mailbox. You'll receive an email invitation when you're invited to a Zoom meeting. Find and click the invitation email in your mailbox.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1a/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-1.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"548\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li>\n<li>Click the invitation link in the email. If you have already downloaded Zoom to your computer, <b>this will automatically connect you to the meeting</b>. If this is your first time using Zoom, read on to learn how to download the necessary software to your computer.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c7/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-2.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"544\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>On some invites, you can find the link to join next to \"Join from PC, Mac, Linux, iOS or Android\" in the email's body text. This will open the Zoom website.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Click on \"download here\" if a download doesn't start automatically.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9a/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-3.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"543\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>If you're prompted, click <b>Launch Application</b> in the pop-up window. This will automatically prompt you to download the Zoom launcher to your computer.</li>\n<li>This will cause the \"zoomuslauncher.zip\" file to automatically download onto your computer.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Double click the downloaded file to install Zoom. This will open the contents of the \"zoomuslauncher.zip\" file.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/5f/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-4.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>Click <b>Continue</b>, if prompted, to install Zoom.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Reopen your email and click on the meeting link again. This should automatically connect you to the meeting.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/21/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-5.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"544\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>If it doesn't, open the Zoom app that you just downloaded, click on <b>Join a Meeting</b> and enter the meeting link or ID.</li>\n<li>If the host has not started the meeting yet, you'll see a message stating \"Please wait for the host to start this meeting\" at the top.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Click the green  button. This button should automatically appear once you join the meeting. It will connect you to the meeting with your microphone.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/97/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-6.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"543\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li>\n<li>Click the  button on the bottom-left (optional). This button looks like a video camera icon in the lower-left corner of the meeting window. It will allow the other participants to view your computer's camera.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/02/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-7.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"549\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li></ol>\n<h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac&#38;action=edit&#38;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Using a Meeting ID or Link to Join a Call\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Using-a-Meeting-ID-or-Link-to-Join-a-Call\">Using a Meeting ID or Link to Join a Call</span></h3>\n<ol><li>Open the <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external text\" href=\"https://zoom.us\">Zoom</a> website in your internet browser. Type <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external text\" href=\"https://zoom.us\">https://zoom.us</a> into your browser's address bar, and hit  or  on your keyboard.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bb/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-8.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li>\n<li>Click the  button on the top-right. You can find it near the blue <b>SIGN UP, IT'S FREE</b> button in the upper-right corner of the page.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/de/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-9.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>If you're signed in, you'll see <b>MY ACCOUNT</b> instead of the sign-up button here.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Enter the meeting ID or link into the text field. You can get the meeting ID or link from the meeting's host.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/af/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-10.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>If you have an invitation email, you can also find the meeting ID here.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Click the blue  button. This will find your meeting from your meeting ID or link, and connect you here.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/58/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-11.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>You'll see a message that says \"Launching\" on your screen.</li>\n<li>If the meeting doesn't automatically launch, click the blue <b>click here</b> link, and then click <b>join from your browser</b>.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Enter your display name for the meeting. Click the <b>Your Name</b> field, and enter a name here. You will connect to the meeting with the name you enter here.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1a/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-12.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"544\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div>\n<ul><li>If you're logged in, you may automatically skip this step.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Click the blue  button. This will connect your audio to the meeting, and open the meeting screen in a new tab. You can now use your microphone, and start talking with your colleagues in the meeting.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/ba/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-13.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"544\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li>\n<li>Click the  button on the bottom-left. This button looks like a video camera icon in the lower-left corner of your screen. It will turn your camera on, and allow the other participants to view your video.<div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-14.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Join a Zoom Meeting on PC or Mac Step 14.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bb/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-14.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-14.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"549\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a></div></li></ol>\n<h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" humb/0/02/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-7.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-7.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-31-640_f20d140ee1e1d213.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bb/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-8.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-8.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn43@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-32-734_9eace8367d577435.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/de/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-9.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn32@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-49-109_94db4bb6804babdf.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/af/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-10.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn83@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-31-654_464be852ab52064b.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/58/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-11.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn52@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-33-712_8f746663c72e21cd.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1a/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-12.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn95@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-32-964_8b7865674be91e04.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/ba/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-13.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-13.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn67@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-31-655_d204eeccad2bca9d.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bb/Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-14.jpg/aid10789466-v4-728px-Join-a-Zoom-Meeting-on-PC-or-Mac-Step-14.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn52@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-32-793_457bc95aae9e6969.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381483030},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","title":"How to Clean a Rusty Necklace","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Rusty or tarnished jewelry can look dull and not quite as pretty as new jewelry. Rust looks reddish and flaky and usually shows up on costume jewelry, while tarnish appears dull and usually affects silver jewelry. You can clean your rusty or tarnished necklace with a few items that you probably already have in your home to clean up your jewelry and look dazzling all night long. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Cleaning with Vinegar\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Cleaning-with-Vinegar\">Cleaning with Vinegar</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Fill a bowl with of white vinegar. White vinegar is a natural cleaning agent that is mildly acidic, but not so much that it will hurt your necklace. Pour some into a bowl or a shallow dish that is large enough to hold your necklace.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can find white vinegar at most home goods or grocery stores.</li> \n    <li>Vinegar won’t harm costume jewelry, but it may hurt any precious metals or stones.</li> \n    <li>Vinegar is great at removing rust, but won't work as well on tarnish.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Submerge your necklace in the vinegar completely. Make sure all parts of your necklace are dunked underneath the vinegar, especially the areas with rust on them. If you need to, add more vinegar so that your necklace is entirely covered.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Let your necklace sit for about 8 hours. Vinegar takes time to loosen the rust attached to your necklace. Set your bowl in an area where it won’t be disturbed overnight and check on it in the morning.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>Scrub off the rust with a toothbrush. Pick your necklace out of the vinegar and set it down on a towel. Use a toothbrush to gently rub the rust off your necklace until it’s clean again. If there’s a lot of rust on your necklace, you can let it sit for another 1 to 2 hours to soak.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>A toothbrush has soft bristles that won’t scratch your necklace.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Rinse off your necklace with cool water. Make sure all of the vinegar is gone so that it doesn’t break down parts of your necklace. Focus the water on any areas that were especially rusty to clean them.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Cool water is more gentle on your jewelry than warm water is.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pat your necklace dry with a clean cloth. Make sure your necklace is completely dry before you wear it or store it again. If your necklace is wet, it could get rusty again. Use a clean cloth so you don’t scratch your jewelry.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup><br /><br />\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Clean a Rusty Necklace Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3c/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace-Step-6.jpg/aid11789151-v4-728px-Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Using Dish Soap\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Using-Dish-Soap\">Using Dish Soap</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Mix 2 drops of dish soap with of warm water. Use a small bowl to combine warm water from the sink with some mild dish soap. Try to use unscented, dye-free dish soap if you can to protect the surface of your necklace.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Rub your necklace in the soap and water with your fingers. Dunk your necklace and chain into the water and make sure it’s fully submerged. Gently rub the surface of the pendant and the chain to get rid of any rust or tarnish.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Using your fingers is more gentle than a cloth or a sponge, which can scratch delicate jewelry.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Rinse your necklace under warm water. Make sure there is no soap residue left on your necklace so that it doesn’t leave any dark spots. Use warm water to clean off any extra tarnished areas.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Dry dish soap can discolor your necklace and make it look spotty.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pat your necklace dry with a clean cloth. Make sure your cloth is completely free from dirt and debris before you use it. Gently pat your necklace and make sure it is fully dry before you put it away.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Storing your necklace while it’s wet can lead to more rust or tarnish.</li> \n    <li>If your necklace is silver, buff some silver polish into its surface to keep it shiny.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Mixing Baking Soda and Salt\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Mixing-Baking-Soda-and-Salt\">Mixing Baking Soda and Salt</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Line a small bowl with aluminum foil. Keep the shiny side of the foil up. Choose a bowl that can hold about of liquid.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Aluminum foil creates an electrolytic reaction to remove tarnish and rust without harming the metal of the necklace.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Mix 1 tbsp (14 g) of baking soda and 1 tbsp (14 g) of table salt with warm water. Heat up of warm water in the microwave until it is hot but not boiling. Pour the water in the bowl with the foil and then stir in the baking soda and table salt until they have dissolved completely.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Baking soda is a natural cleaning agent that is mildly corrosive. It can remove tarnish from gold and silver, and rust from steel or costume jewelry.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Submerge your necklace in the mixture and make sure it touches the foil. Use caution as you place your necklace in the bowl since the water will still be hot. Make sure the necklace touches the bottom of the bowl so it’s in contact with the foil.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Let the necklace sit for 2 to 10 minutes. Depending on how tarnished or rusty your necklace is, you may need to let it sit for the full 10 minutes. You may notice some small bubbles on your necklace, which is just the chemical reaction removing the rust.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If your necklace wasn’t super rusty, you can take it out after 2 or 3 minutes.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Rinse your necklace with cold water. Use tongs to pick your necklace out of the hot water and then clean it off in the sink with cool water. Make sure there is no residue of the salt or baking soda so they don’t sit on your necklace long term.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup><br /><br /></li> \n  <li>Pat the necklace dry with a clean cloth. Set your necklace on a cloth laid flat and gently fold it over to pat the necklace dry. Leave the necklace out to air dry for 1 hour before you store it again to prevent rust, or put your necklace on right away to enjoy its new, shiny look.<sup id=\"_ref-16\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 16\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace#_note-16\">[16]</a></sup> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Rust builds up on necklaces when they are left in a moist or wet environment.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Video\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Video\">Video</span></h2> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Things You'll Need\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Things-You'll-Need\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Things-You.27ll-Need\">Things You'll Need</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Cleaning with Vinegar\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Cleaning-with-Vinegar_2\">Cleaning with Vinegar</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>Bowl</li> \n  <li>Distilled white vinegar</li> \n  <li>Soft-bristled brush or toothbrush</li> \n  <li>Soft cloth</li>\n </ul> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Using Dish Soap\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Using-Dish-Soap_2\">Using Dish Soap</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>Small bowl</li> \n  <li>Dish soap</li> \n  <li>Soft cloth</li>\n </ul> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Mixing Baking Soda and Salt\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Mixing-Baking-Soda-and-Salt_2\">Mixing Baking Soda and Salt</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>Aluminum foil</li> \n  <li>Baking soda</li> \n  <li>Table salt</li> \n  <li>Microwave</li> \n  <li>Soft cloth</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Never clean jewelry with precious gemstones or pearls in it. The cleaning solution can damage gemstones and pearls.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Clean-a-Rusty-Necklace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11\" title=\"Edit section: References\">Edit</a><span Summary\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Quick-Summary\">Quick Summary</span></h2>\n <div class=\"mw-references-wrap class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>This wikiHow will teach you how to activate the camera app in Windows 10 as well as how to give other apps permission to use your camera. Many Windows 10 computers come with built-in webcams, such as all-in-one desktops and laptops. If you need to buy a webcam for a PC without a built-in webcam, you can refer to <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Buy-a-Webcam\" title=\"Buy a Webcam\">How to Buy a Webcam</a> and <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Set-up-a-Webcam\" title=\"Set up a Webcam\">How to Set up a Webcam</a>. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Using the Camera Application\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Using-the-Camera-Application\">Using the Camera Application</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Press . You can press this key with the Windows logo to open the Start menu, but you can also click the Windows logo in your Start menu.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Activate the Camera in Windows 10 Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/32/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-1.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Click . It's in the \"C\" section of listed apps.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Activate the Camera in Windows 10 Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8f/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-2.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Click to change the settings and take a video instead of a picture. You can press this key with the Windows logo to open the Start menu, but you can also click the Windows logo in your Start menu.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Activate the Camera in Windows 10 Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/23/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-4.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Click . You'll see this gear icon on the left side of the menu.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Activate the Camera in Windows 10 Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/49/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-5.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Click . It's at the bottom of the menu next to an icon of a padlock.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Activate the Camera in Windows 10 Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8a/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-6.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Click . You'll find this menu option in the menu on the left side of the window under the header \"App permissions.\"\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Activate the Camera in Windows 10 Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/50/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-7.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Click the toggle on under \"Allow apps to access your camera.<b>\"</b> This setting will allow any apps you install access to your camera.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" \n  </ol>\n </div> \n</div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Mon, 02 Nov 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/32/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-1.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-1.jpg","linkMd5":"7ea1e314c2a06313e5c4a979c0bd402e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn19@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-23-515_030fb9643bb093ac.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":546,"sourceBytes":28360,"destBytes":13060,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/32/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-1.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-1.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn19@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-23-515_030fb9643bb093ac.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8f/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-2.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn71@2020_3/2020/11/03/05-31-31-779_9e0b58733e5d0fd7.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f5/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-3.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-3.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn71@2020_3/2020/11/03/05-31-31-622_ddfefb0641ebb643.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/23/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-4.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-4.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn59@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-33-612_abb50931a6300dbe.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/49/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-5.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-5.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn32@2020_3/2020/11/03/05-31-32-663_b9c09abf3c8b1bb9.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8a/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-6.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-6.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn60@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-31-635_9adc537f7bb11ed4.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/50/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-7.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-7.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn71@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-33-723_e16ed81bd4ed529e.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1d/Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-8.jpg/aid12175909-v4-728px-Activate-the-Camera-in-Windows-10-Step-8.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx21/cdn28@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-33-252_e3ea654942b408b8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381483031},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","title":"How to Roast Pumpkin Seeds","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Instead of throwing out the pumpkin seeds after a pumpkin carving session, try roasting them as a delicious snack instead! Rinse the seeds under cold running water before drying them and baking them in the oven until they're golden brown. You can add any sort of seasonings you desire, turning your pumpkin seeds into a spicy, sweet, or simply flavorful treat. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Removing the Seeds from the Pumpkin\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Removing-the-Seeds-from-the-Pumpkin\">Removing the Seeds from the Pumpkin</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Remove the top of the pumpkin to access the seeds. If you haven’t already done so, use a sharp cutting knife to cut a circle around the pumpkin’s stem. Make sure the lid is wide enough for your hand to fit through comfortably. Remove the lid once you’re done cutting it.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-1-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 1 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/4a/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-1-Version-5.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-1-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Use a large spoon to scoop the seeds from the pumpkin. The bigger the spoon, the more seeds you’ll be able to remove at once. Scrape the sides of the pumpkin to loosen the seeds and pulp, taking time to scoop out as many seeds as possible.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can also use your hands or an object from a pumpkin carving kit.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Place all of the seeds and pulp in a large bowl. As you’re scooping out the seeds, place the seeds and pulp in a bowl big enough to hold everything. Remove large pieces of pulp from the seeds as you’re placing them in the bowl, but don’t worry about separating every single string.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-3-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 3 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/7c/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-3-Version-5.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-3-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re removing the seeds from a smaller pumpkin, you may not need as large of a bowl.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Washing and Drying the Seeds\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Washing-and-Drying-the-Seeds\">Washing and Drying the Seeds</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Set the seeds in a colander and rinse them under cold water. This will help loosen the pulp and strings from the seeds, making it easier to clean them. Hold the colander full of seeds under the running water, using your hands to move the seeds around gently.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-4-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 4 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/38/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-4-Version-5.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-4-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Pull the seeds out of the colander and place them on a towel. Once the seeds are mostly clean, take them out of the colander and set them on a clean kitchen towel. If there are any big strings still attached to the seeds, pull these off if possible.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-5-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 5 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/b2/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-5-Version-5.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-5-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can also place the seeds on paper towels, though they may stick.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pat the seeds dry using the kitchen towel. Spread the seeds out on the towel and gently blot the seeds to ensure they’re as dry as possible. Place the seeds in a bowl once they’re dry.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Instead of blotting the seeds, you can also shake them in the colander to remove excess water.</li> \n    <li>If the seeds are still damp when they go in the oven, they won’t roast well due to the moisture.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Adding Seasonings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Adding-Seasonings\">Adding Seasonings</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Toss the seeds with oil or butter. Once the clean, dry seeds are in a bowl, pour cooking oil or melted butter into the bowl so that the seeds are lightly covered. Use a large spoon to mix the seeds around with the oil or butter so that each seed is covered evenly.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Use canola oil, olive oil, or vegetable oil.</li> \n    <li>How much oil or butter you use will depend on how many pumpkin seeds you’re roasting, but it’s best to start with a small amount—you can always add more.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Add your desired seasonings. These could be seasonings such as Worcestershire sauce, garlic powder, paprika, salt, pepper—whichever seasonings are your favorite. Sprinkle the desired amount of seasoning into the bowl of pumpkin seeds.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup><br /><br /> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Experiment with the type and amount of seasonings, sprinkling in small amounts before adding more.</li> \n    <li>For a simple yet tasty flavor, just add salt and pepper to your pumpkin seeds.</li> \n    <li>Consider adding seasonings like chili powder, Cajun seasoning, or crab seasoning for a stronger flavor.</li> \n    <li>Season with sugar, cinnamon, and nutmeg for a sweet snack.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Stir the pumpkin seed mixture thoroughly using a large spoon. Stir gently, making sure the pumpkin seeds are evenly coated with oil or butter and your desired seasonings. If you notice that many seeds don’t have seasoning on them, feel free to sprinkle a little bit more into the mixture.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup><br /><br /></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Baking the Seeds\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Baking-the-Seeds\">Baking the Seeds</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Preheat the oven to and prepare a sheet pan. Lining your baking sheet with parchment paper will prevent the seeds from sticking the best, though you can also use aluminum foil. Once the oven is preheated, you're ready to roast your seeds.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-10-Version-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 10 Version 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3a/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-10-Version-5.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-10-Version-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Spread the seeds out evenly on the baking sheet. Pour the seasoned pumpkin seeds onto the lined baking sheet, using a spoon to spread them out. Try to make sure they aren’t clumped together and are laying flat so they roast evenly.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-11-Version-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 11 Version 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/9a/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-11-Version-4.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-11-Version-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If your pumpkin seeds end up layered on top of one another, try baking them in two smaller batches to promote even roasting.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Bake the seeds for 20-30 minutes, stirring them occasionally. Remove the baking sheet from the oven every 10 minutes and move the seeds around using a wooden spoon or other kitchen utensil—this will help ensure each seed roasts evenly. Once the seeds look browned, they’re done!<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fa/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-12.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Eat the seeds warm or let them cool to room temperature. Once the seeds have been removed and the oven is turned off, use a spatula to scoop the seeds into a bowl or other serving dish. You can eat them while they’re still warm from the oven, or let them sit for a few minutes until they’re cool.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/63/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-13.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Store the seeds in an airtight container for roughly 1 week. If you want to save your roasted pumpkin seeds, put them in an airtight container such as a mason jar, plastic bag, or piece of tupperware. The seeds will stay fresh for a week or so at room temperature, or you can place them in the freezer for up to a month.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-14.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Roast Pumpkin Seeds Step 14.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/71/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-14.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-14.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"410\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If placing the seeds in the freezer, they should be in an airtight container as well.</li> \n    <li>Write the date on the container so you remember when the seeds were roasted.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Things You'll Need\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Things-You'll-Need\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Things-You.27ll-Need\">Things You'll Need</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Cutting knife</li> \n  <li>Large spoon</li> \n  <li>Large bowl</li> \n  <li>Colander</li> \n  <li>Towel</li> \n  <li>Oil or butter</li> \n  <li>Seasonings</li> \n  <li>Sheet pan</li> \n  <li>Parchment paper or aluminum foil</li> \n  <li>Airtight container (optional)</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Video\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Video\">Video</span></h2> \n <p>This video shows you a different way to roast pumpkin seeds. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Place newspaper over your table surfaces for easier cleanup.</li> \n  <li>The pumpkin seeds can also be added to a <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Salad\" title=\"Make a Salad\">salad</a> or <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Pumpkin-Soup\" title=\"Make Pumpkin Soup\">soup</a>.</li> \n  <li>Add your seasonings after roasting the seeds, if desired.</li> \n  <li>Try using a toaster oven for smaller amounts of pumpkin seeds.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Related wikiHows\">Edit</a><span
