8px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn64@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-32-761_8df37d0f9bbad0b9.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/63/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-13.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-13.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn14@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-31-640_a7b60a144232df47.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/71/Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-14.jpg/aid13695-v4-728px-Roast-Pumpkin-Seeds-Step-14.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn76@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-33-807_e2944d10f0a35ba8.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381483031},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","title":"How to Tell Scary Stories","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Before horror movies laced with special effects kept people up at night, people got scared the old-fashioned way: through storytelling. Telling scary stories in a way that really scares people can be tough to master, so it does take some practice. You can come up with the perfect story and build suspense to keep your audience hooked on your every word. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Tell-Scary-Stories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Tell-Scary-Stories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Coming up with a Story\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Coming-up-with-a-Story\">Coming up with a Story</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Read a few classic scary stories to get inspiration. Go to the library or search online for the scariest stories you can find. Pick out 3 to 5 stories that have spooking potential and read them all the way through. Think about how you can make them your own by putting your own twist on them.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 1 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/70/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-1-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li><i>Dracula</i>, <i>Frankenstein</i>, and <i>The Woman in Black</i> are a few classic scary stories that you could read.</li> \n    <li>The more realistic and recent the story, the scarier it'll be when you tell it. That way, the listeners can relate.</li> \n    <li>Urban legends make excellent scary stories. The danger with using an urban legend, however, is that some of your listeners may have heard variations of it, thus ruining the effect.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Set the story in a recent time period or place. Change the details so that it seems as though the story took place nearby, and recently. If the story took place in a canning factory, but you know there's a pecan factory in your town, switch out that detail (if you can do so without changing the story too much). If you can tie the story to someone you know, that’s even better.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 2 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/95/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-2-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Add in details to make your story sound realistic. Try to put in as many details as you can so your story sounds real, like where exactly it was, what time of day it was, or what the weather was like. If your story is about you, add in your reactions and what you were feeling. If you’re telling it from someone else’s perspective, give details on who they are and how you found out about it. For the big climax of your story, put in an actionable detail that’s super scary.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 3 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/91/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-3-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, you could tell an urban legend about your hometown from the point of view of your grandpa as a child.</li> \n    <li>Or, you could tell a ghost story about how you explored an abandoned building in the countryside.</li> \n    <li>You can also tweak your story to add in details of your current surroundings. For example, if you’re sitting outside on a foggy night, say that your story happened during a foggy night too.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>End with a frightening climax to your story. The scariest part of a scary story is not knowing what’s coming next. Think of a large, expressive action that will make your audience jump or get super scared. Emphasize how scared the person in your story was to give your audience a way to relate.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 4 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d6/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re telling a story about a monster, the climax could be that it almost caught you as you were running away.</li> \n    <li>If your story involves ghosts, you could talk about how you saw a dark figure in the hallway that rushed towards you.</li> \n    <li>For stories involving creepy critters, describe the feeling of a snake or a spider crawling up your arm.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Practice saying the story out loud once or twice. There’s nothing worse than realizing you forgot a crucial detail in the setup of your story. Spend a few minutes rehearsing how you’re going to tell your story, and make sure you aren’t leaving out any important information.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-5-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 5 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e6/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-5-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-5-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you need to, you can write out a few notes to help you keep track of the details. However, try to memorize your story before you actually tell it.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Tell-Scary-Stories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Building Suspense\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Building-Suspense\">Building Suspense</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Mention some casual details about your story throughout the day. Way before you tell the story (like the day before, or that morning), find a way to mention a few details that are relevant to the story. If you drive by the pecan factory, for example, ask your friends if they've ever been there. If you’re telling a ghost story, ask your friends if they believe in evil spirits.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 6 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f9/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-6-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This will make your audience curious and set up a little suspense before you even start telling your story.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Pick a time when you have your audience’s full attention. If you’re going camping, wait until you’re sitting by the bonfire. If you’re at a sleepover, time your story for when your friends are all in the living room. Try to make them sit around you so you can look everyone in the face.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-7-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 7 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d4/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-7-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-7-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If your audience members are distracted, your story won’t be as effective.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Act nervous about telling the story to build suspense. When the time draws near to tell the story, start pretending to be anxious. Get the chills here and there, and rub your upper arms as if to warm yourself. Look suddenly behind you, or at the distance, as if you just saw something. Keep doing this kind of stuff subtly until someone notices. At first, brush it off as if it's nothing, but keep up the act.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 8 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ea/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-8-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-8-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This will intrigue your audience so that they’re dying to know more. It also helps to build suspense, making your story even scarier.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Tell-Scary-Stories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Scaring Your Audience\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Scaring-Your-Audience\">Scaring Your Audience</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Start telling your story in a slow, quiet voice. Make your voice loud enough so that everyone can hear, but keep your eyes down to make it seem like you’re being forced to talk. A quiet voice can make you seem reluctant, like you don’t want to tell your story but the audience is twisting your arm.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/26/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-9.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This might even force some people to lean in closer to you, giving you more of their attention.</li> \n    <li>You could start your story with something like, “When I was 5 years old, my grandpa told me the story of the bloody lagoon.”</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Add in body language to make your story more realistic. If you’re talking about how scared you were, open your eyes wide to look frightened. If you’re talking about how you had to hit or punch at something, swing your arms wildly. Use your body as a storytelling device to drive home the details.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1d/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-10.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This will help keep your audience engaged and interested in what you have to say.</li> \n    <li>If you’re sitting right next to someone, use caution when you swing your arms around so you don’t hit them.</li> \n    <li>Try to stay seated when you tell your story. Standing up or acting out your words can make you seem too eager.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use pauses for dramatic effect. As you get closer and closer to the climax of your story, stop talking for 2 to 3 seconds at a time. Act like you can’t even bear to tell the rest of the story to engage your audience even more.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8b/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-11.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Your audience might even feel bad for making you tell the story, which makes it even more scary.</li> \n    <li>For example, you could say, “And then… (dramatic pause) I heard a knock at the door.”</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>End the story with the dramatic climax. Yell the last sentence of your story while you lunge forward at your listeners and scare the life out of them. This will probably make them jump since they are so frightened. Even if they chuckle afterwards, you’ll know that you got them good with your story.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Tell-Scary-Stories#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Tell Scary Stories Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/07/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-12.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>You can also end your story as quietly and uncomfortably as you started it for a more subtle, disconcerting effect.</li> \n    <li>Try to keep your story under 5 minutes long so that your audience doesn’t get bored.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Tell-Scary-Stories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Don't smile or laugh when you're telling the story. You want to establish a somber mood, tinged with anxiety.</li> \n  <li>Always be on the lookout for new material. Read horror stories often, and think of ways you can adapt them into the spoken form.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Tell-Scary-Stories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Make sure your story is appropriate for the audience. Young children, for example, probably don’t want to hear about blood and guts.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Tell-Scary-Stories&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Related wikiHows\">Edit</a><span +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/70/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-1-Version-2.jpg","linkMd5":"45b09fb3f5f65ec7a199f8943701fdd5","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn11@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-23-520_9ff2db7bd5af436a.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":546,"sourceBytes":54938,"destBytes":34020,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/70/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-1-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-1-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn11@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-23-520_9ff2db7bd5af436a.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/95/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-2-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-2-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn20@2020_3/2020/11/03/05-31-32-626_773201ce834d3105.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/91/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-3-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-3-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn67@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-49-215_923a6b5b10dde066.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d6/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-4-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx30/cdn55@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-33-580_10dc877ae8f637ba.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e6/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-5-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-5-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn16@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-33-288_d392b178d6ee2245.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/f9/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-6-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-6-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn48@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-33-614_a3232051753ddec6.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/d4/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-7-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-7-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn12@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-31-620_d03354dc7998f183.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/ea/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-8-Version-2.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-8-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx22/cdn47@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-32-720_13c1f804981d2edd.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/2/26/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-9.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-9.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn28@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-31-944_aa27fa1541742a52.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/1d/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-10.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-10.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn79@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-32-957_11e940bb3760a2f5.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8b/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-11.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-11.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn99@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-31-518_7e8e699da121752b.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/07/Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-12.jpg/aid386748-v4-728px-Tell-Scary-Stories-Step-12.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn99@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-33-093_153f278002e83d4f.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381483031},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","title":"How to Change a Name With the Credit Bureaus","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>If your legal name changes because of a marriage, divorce or other court order, it is wise to contact the credit bureaus directly to notify them of the change. When you update your name with your creditors, they will automatically notify the credit reporting agencies. But this can take a lot of time, sometimes up to six months or more. This could delay any loan application process or other credit history review. Instead, be proactive and notify the credit reporting agencies yourself of your name change. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Notifying the Credit Reporting Agencies\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Notifying-the-Credit-Reporting-Agencies\">Notifying the Credit Reporting Agencies</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Contact all 3 credit bureaus with your updated information. When you change your name with your creditors and with Social Security, the credit agencies should be automatically notified of the change. However, it’s still a good idea to send them a letter informing them of the change.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Resign-Gracefully-Step-12-Version-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Resign Gracefully Step 12 Version 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bd/Resign-Gracefully-Step-12-Version-3.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Resign-Gracefully-Step-12-Version-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Send your information to Equifax at P.O. Box 740256, Atlanta, GA 30374</li> \n    <li>Get in touch with TransUnion LLC P.O. Box 2000, Chester, PA 19022</li> \n    <li>Let Experian know about your name change. Send information to National Consumer Assistance Center, P.O. Box 2002, Allen, TX 75013.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Include relevant information in the letter. The credit reporting agencies will need specific documentation in order to process your name change. In addition to your previous and new names, they will need your contact information and legal verification of your name change.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Conduct-Research-Step-23.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Conduct Research Step 23.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e9/Conduct-Research-Step-23.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Conduct-Research-Step-23.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Tell them your name. In your letter, let the agency know your full previous full name as well as your new full name.</li> \n    <li>Inform them of a new address. If your address has changed, let the agency know both your old and new legal address.</li> \n    <li>Include your social security number on the letter. To make sure they are changing the information for the correct person, include your social security number on the letter. This number separates you from any other person out there with your same name.</li> \n    <li>Enclose proof of your legal name change. Provide in your envelope any legal documentation you have concerning your name change. This documentation may include a marriage license, official divorce papers or other court order.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Get your credit report. Obtain a copy of your credit report as a follow up to your name change request with the credit bureaus. According to the Fair Credit Reporting Act (FCRA), you are entitled to receive a free credit report once every 12 months. You can also purchase a copy of your credit report from the credit reporting agencies.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Write-a-Grant-Proposal-Step-17-Version-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Write a Grant Proposal Step 17 Version 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fd/Write-a-Grant-Proposal-Step-17-Version-3.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Write-a-Grant-Proposal-Step-17-Version-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Visit <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external text\" href=\"http://www.annualcreditreport.com/\">AnnualCreditReport.com</a> or call 1-877-322-8228. You can also download the <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external text\" href=\"http://www.consumer.ftc.gov/articles/pdf-0093-annual-report-request-form.pdf\">Annual Credit Report Request Form</a> and mail it to Annual Credit Report Request Service, P.O. Box 105281, Atlanta, GA 30348-5281.</li> \n    <li>If you have already received your free credit report within the past 12 months, you can purchase a copy from <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external text\" href=\"http://www.equifax.com/3in1-credit-report-score/\">Equifax</a> for $39.95. This includes your credit history from all three credit reporting agencies and your FICO score.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup></li> \n    <li>You can purchase a credit report from one of the credit reporting agencies for $19.95 from <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external text\" href=\"http://www.myfico.com/\">myFICO</a>.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup></li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Understand how a name change affects your credit history. Changing your name should not change your credit history. Your credit should just continue to build in your new name. Your old and new names should be included on your credit report. \n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Reduce-Your-Student-Loan-Payments-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Reduce Your Student Loan Payments Step 6 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a7/Reduce-Your-Student-Loan-Payments-Step-6-Version-2.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Reduce-Your-Student-Loan-Payments-Step-6-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>When your last name changes after a marriage or divorce, your credit reports automatically update after you notify your creditors of your new name. As creditors update their records, they send the changes to the credit reporting agencies.</li> \n    <li>If you change your whole name, it is possible that creditors will have trouble verifying your credit history. This is because credit reporting agencies identify you not just with your Social Security number, but also with your date of birth and current and previous mailing addresses. When applying for credit under your new name, be sure to provide full and complete identifying information so the credit reporting agencies can link you to your credit history.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Notifying Creditors of Name Change\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Notifying-Creditors-of-Name-Change\">Notifying Creditors of Name Change</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Get a new Social Security card. Do this first because you can use it to officially change your name on other forms of identification. Only your name will change, not your social security number. You will need to include proof of your age, identity, and U.S. citizenship or immigration status.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-22.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Change Your Name in Texas Step 22.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8c/Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-22.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-22.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Download the <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external text\" href=\"http://www.socialsecurity.gov/forms/ss-5.pdf\">Application for a New Social Security Card</a> from the Social Security Administration.</li> \n    <li>Provide proof of your age, such as your birth certificate, a U.S. hospital record of your birth (created at the time of birth), a religious record established before age five showing your age or date of birth, your passport, or a final adoption decree (the adoption decree must show that the birth information was taken from the original.</li> \n    <li>Include proof of identity, such as a U.S. driver's license, a U.S. State-issued non-driver identity card or a U.S. passport.</li> \n    <li>Include evidence of U.S. citizenship, such as a U.S. birth certificate, a U.S. Passport, a consular report of birth, a certificate of citizenship or a certificate of naturalization.</li> \n    <li>If you are not a U.S. citizen, include an unexpired document issued to you by the Department of Homeland Security (DHS) showing your immigration status, such as Form I-551, I-94, or I-766. International students or exchange visitors must also submit Form I-20, DS-2019 or a letter from their school or employer authorizing their employment (F-1) or sponsorship (J-1).</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Change your name on your driver’s license. Once you have your new Social Security card, you can use it to change your name on your driver’s license. Visit the website of your states Department of Motor Vehicles to learn the process for changing your name on your driver’s license. You will likely need to bring your social security card, your old driver’s license, your birth certificate, and legal verification of your name change, such as a marriage license, official divorce papers or other court order.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-23.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Change Your Name in Texas Step 23.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/4b/Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-23.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-23.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Change your name with your employer. Your employer’s human resources department will assist you with changing your name on your work documents. You need to do this so that your paychecks and pay stubs reflect your new name. Other work documents, such as your life insurance and retirement plan documents, should also be updated with your new name.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Get-a-Job-Fast-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Get a Job Fast Step 4 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/de/Get-a-Job-Fast-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Get-a-Job-Fast-Step-4-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li> \n  <li>Update your name on your financial accounts. Notify all of your banks and creditors of your new name. When you notify your creditors of your new name, they will automatically notify the credit bureaus. Your credit history under your old name will not be erased or changed. Rather, your credit will just continue to build under your new name.\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Close-a-Bank-Account-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Close a Bank Account Step 3 Version 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3b/Close-a-Bank-Account-Step-3-Version-2.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Close-a-Bank-Account-Step-3-Version-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>To update your name on your bank accounts, you may need to visit your bank in person. Bring your social security number, driver’s license or passport, and legal verification of your name change, such as a marriage license, divorce decree or court order. Change you name on your credit cards, debit cards and checks. If your name has changed because you got married or divorced, you may need to add or remove a spouse from ownership on your accounts.</li> \n    <li>Notify other creditors of your name change, including issuers of a car loan, line of credit, mortgage, credit cards and other credit accounts.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Fixing Errors on Your Credit Report\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Fixing-Errors-on-Your-Credit-Report\">Fixing Errors on Your Credit Report</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Contact the credit bureau. If you receive your credit report and you find that your name is incorrectly reported, contact them right away. Send a letter by certified mail, return receipt requested so that you can track it. Include copies of all of your supporting documents, including your identification, Social Security card and legal verification of your name change.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Obtain-a-Copy-of-Your-Birth-Certificate-in-Ohio-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Obtain a Copy of Your Birth Certificate in Ohio Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/57/Obtain-a-Copy-of-Your-Birth-Certificate-in-Ohio-Step-6.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Obtain-a-Copy-of-Your-Birth-Certificate-in-Ohio-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Send the letter to Equifax at Equifax Information Services, LLC, P.O. Box 740256, Atlanta, GA 30374.</li> \n    <li>Send the letter to TransUnion at P.O. Box 2000, Chester, PA 19022-2000.</li> \n    <li>Send the letter to Experian at P.O. Box 2002, Allen, TX 75013.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Contact the agency that reporting the inaccurate information. If you have any inaccuracy on your credit report, contact the creditor or other agency who reported the incorrect information. Work with them to update their documentation to accurately reflect your new legal name. Notify them that you have contacted the credit bureaus to report the inaccuracy.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Ends-Meet-Step-13.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Ends Meet Step 13.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a3/Make-Ends-Meet-Step-13.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Make-Ends-Meet-Step-13.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"http://www.consumer.ftc.gov/articles/0155-free-credit-reports\">http://www.consumer.ftc.gov/articles/0155-free-credit-reports</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_ref-4\">↑</a> <span class=\"reference-text\"><a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"http://www.equifax.com/3in1-credit-report-score/\">http://www.equifax.com/3in1-credit-report-score/</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_ref-5\">↑</a> <span class=\"reference-text\"><a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"http://www.myfico.com/\">http://www.myfico.com/</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_ref-6\">↑</a> <span class=\"reference-text\"><a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"http://www.socialsecurity.gov/forms/ss-5.pdf\">http://www.socialsecurity.gov/forms/ss-5.pdf</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Change-a-Name-With-the-Credit-Bureaus#_ref-7\">↑</a> <span class=\"reference-text\"> <a target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\" class=\"external free\" href=\"http://www.myfico.com/crediteducation/rights/fixinganerror.aspx\">http://www.myfico.com/crediteducation/rights/fixinganerror.aspx</a></span> </li> \n   <li id=\"_note-8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"http://www.myfico.com/crediteducation/rights/fixinganerror.aspx\">http://www.myfico.com/crediteducation/rights/fixinganerror.aspx</a></span> </li> \n  </ol>\n </div> \n</div>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Sat, 31 Oct 2020 16:00:00 +0000","feedId":44,"bgimg":"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bd/Resign-Gracefully-Step-12-Version-3.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Resign-Gracefully-Step-12-Version-3.jpg","linkMd5":"db14e41176c6136b5a6edcf9370a9210","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn4@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-23-536_17c089bda0cd8036.webp","destWidth":728,"destHeight":546,"sourceBytes":42811,"destBytes":24586,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/b/bd/Resign-Gracefully-Step-12-Version-3.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Resign-Gracefully-Step-12-Version-3.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn4@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-23-536_17c089bda0cd8036.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e9/Conduct-Research-Step-23.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Conduct-Research-Step-23.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn55@2020_1/2020/11/03/05-31-31-554_16a7eade81c09781.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/f/fd/Write-a-Grant-Proposal-Step-17-Version-3.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Write-a-Grant-Proposal-Step-17-Version-3.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn44@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-31-875_3d56140190608635.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a7/Reduce-Your-Student-Loan-Payments-Step-6-Version-2.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Reduce-Your-Student-Loan-Payments-Step-6-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn4@2020_4/2020/11/03/05-31-48-399_273eb2f22a47dc42.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/8c/Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-22.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-22.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn40@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-33-519_5e0cf203674d68a4.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/4/4b/Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-23.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Change-Your-Name-in-Texas-Step-23.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn40@2020_5/2020/11/03/05-31-31-594_d555bf36025935bb.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/d/de/Get-a-Job-Fast-Step-4-Version-2.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Get-a-Job-Fast-Step-4-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn100@2020_3/2020/11/03/05-31-32-480_d59133e13f7c1acf.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/3b/Close-a-Bank-Account-Step-3-Version-2.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Close-a-Bank-Account-Step-3-Version-2.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn64@2020_2/2020/11/03/05-31-33-767_88b51cf317ae7022.webp","https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/5/57/Obtain-a-Copy-of-Your-Birth-Certificate-in-Ohio-Step-6.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Obtain-a-Copy-of-Your-Birth-Certificate-in-Ohio-Step-6.jpg":null,"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/a/a3/Make-Ends-Meet-Step-13.jpg/aid1165234-v4-728px-Make-Ends-Meet-Step-13.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn47@2020_6/2020/11/03/05-31-32-693_687d03751953f422.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1604381483029},{"createdTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","updatedTime":"2020-11-03 13:31:23","title":"How to Make Smoked Paprika","link":"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika","description":"<div class=\"mw-parser-output\">\n <p>Smoked paprika provides a big smoky flavor that is an essential component of many dishes that call for it. However, it can also be harder to find in stores than other types of paprika. If you’re cooking something like a Spanish paella that calls for smoked paprika, but you don’t have any on hand, don’t worry! You can probably find an acceptable substitute in your spice cupboard to save the day. On the other hand, if you find yourself cooking with smoked paprika all the time, you can try smoking, dehydrating, and grinding fresh peppers to make your very own homemade batch to have handy. </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1\" title=\"Edit section: Ingredients\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Ingredients\">Ingredients</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2\" title=\"Edit section: Homemade Smoked Paprika\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Homemade-Smoked-Paprika\">Homemade Smoked Paprika</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>fresh capsicum peppers</li>\n </ul> \n <p><i>Makes 3/4 of a cup (86 g) of smoked paprika powder</i> </p> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3\" title=\"Edit section: Steps\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Steps\">Steps</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4\" title=\"Edit section: Creating Your Own Smoked Paprika\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Creating-Your-Own-Smoked-Paprika\">Creating Your Own Smoked Paprika</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Wash and dry red peppers that you want to make smoked paprika with. Use red bell peppers if you want a milder, sweeter paprika or red chili peppers if you want spicy smoked paprika. Rinse your chosen peppers thoroughly under cool running water, then pat them dry with a clean kitchen towel or paper towels or let them air dry completely.<sup id=\"_ref-1\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 1\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-1\">[1]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-1.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 1.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/8/80/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-1.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-1.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Paprika can be made from any capsicum pepper, but the traditional paprika is made from pimiento peppers (small, sweet, red peppers with thin walls)</li> \n    <li>You don’t have to only use red peppers, although this is what gives paprika its rich red color. Feel free to mix some orange or yellow peppers in with some red peppers to create your own unique blend of flavors.</li> \n    <li>Note that of fresh peppers will give you about 3/4 of a cup (86 g) of smoked paprika powder.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Deseed and chop the peppers. Place your peppers one at a time on a cutting board and use a sharp kitchen knife to cut off the top with the stem, then cut out and remove the center and the seeds. Slice each pepper in half, cut out any white ribs, and scrape out any remaining seeds. Cut larger peppers, such as bell peppers, into 4-8 thinner slices.<sup id=\"_ref-2\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 2\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-2\">[2]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-2.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 2.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/1/11/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-2.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-2.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re making your paprika with hot peppers, wear latex gloves while you cut and prepare them to avoid getting the spicy capsicum on your hands.</li> \n    <li>Be very careful not to touch your face, especially your eyes, while you’re preparing your peppers or you might transfer capsicum and experience an unpleasant burning sensation.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use a smoker filled with oak wood chips to smoke the peppers. Soak the oak wood chips in water for at least 15 minutes, then load them into an <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Use-an-Electric-Smoker\" title=\"Use an Electric Smoker\">electric</a> or <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Use-a-Charcoal-Smoker\" title=\"Use a Charcoal Smoker\">charcoal</a> smoker. Put all your prepared peppers in a basket on the smoker’s grill and smoke them for at least 3 hours.<sup id=\"_ref-3\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 3\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-3\">[3]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-3.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 3.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/9/95/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-3.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-3.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Traditional smoked paprika is made by smoking the peppers very slowly over a period of days or weeks until they are totally dry. However, this isn’t really practical if you’re making it at home. You can just smoke them for a few hours to impart the smokey flavor, then finish drying them out using a dehydrator or your oven.</li> \n    <li>If you don’t have a smoker, you can also <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-a-Smoker-Grill\" title=\"Make a Smoker Grill\">use a regular charcoal grill</a> as a smoker.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Dry the peppers out in a food dehydrator or in your oven. Lay the peppers out in an even layer on a food dehydrator tray or a baking tray. Set the dehydrator or oven to , then put the peppers inside and dehydrate them for at least 5 hours, or until they’re completely dry.<sup id=\"_ref-4\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 4\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-4\">[4]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-4.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 4.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e6/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-4.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-4.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you’re using an oven and it doesn’t go down to , just use the lowest temperature it has and check on the peppers every hour or so. If you dry them out at , for example, they might be done after 3 hours.</li> \n    <li>If you’re using a dehydrator and it has a different recommended temperature for dehydrating vegetables, use that instead. Keep in mind that 5 hours is the minimum time your peppers will need in a dehydrator, but you can leave them overnight or for up to 12 hours.</li> \n    <li>Keep in mind that very spicy peppers can give off an intense odor while they’re dehydrating, so open up windows and use a fan for ventilation if you’re drying out hot peppers. If you’re using a portable dehydrator, you can even put it outside if you have room.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Grind the peppers into a powder using an electric blade-style coffee grinder. Transfer the peppers in small batches to the grinder. Put the lid on, turn the grinder on, and blend the peppers up until they turn into a fine, uniform powder. Pour the powder out into a bowl and repeat the process until you grind all the peppers.<sup id=\"_ref-5\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 5\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-5\">[5]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-5.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 5.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/6/6a/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-5.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-5.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Blade-style coffee grinders are also often marketed as herb or spice grinders. They’re the same thing.</li> \n    <li>If your grinder has multiple settings, choose the finest grinding setting.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Sift the powder through a fine mesh strainer to make sure there are no chunks. Place a fine mesh strainer over a bowl and pour all your paprika powder through it. Stir it around with a spoon to break up chunks and help it fall through the strainer until all the powder is in the bowl below. Discard any large pieces, such as bits of skin, that are left in the strainer.<sup id=\"_ref-6\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 6\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-6\">[6]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-6.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 6.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/e/e8/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-6.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-6.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>If you have a lot of bigger pieces left in the strainer, you can try grinding them up again. If you just have a few bits of skin and things like that, go ahead and just throw those pieces away.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Store your smoked paprika in a sealed container at room temperature. Transfer the powder to a sealable container, such as a jar with a screw-on lid, and put the lid on tightly. Put the jar somewhere where it will stay at room temperature, like in a cupboard, away from heat sources like the stove and sunlight.<sup id=\"_ref-7\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 7\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-7\">[7]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-7.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 7.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/c/c6/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-7.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-7.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Paprika doesn’t go bad, but it can lose potency over time, especially when exposed to heat. In general, it will be most potent within 6-8 months of making it.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5\" title=\"Edit section: Using Smoked Paprika Substitutes\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Using-Smoked-Paprika-Substitutes\">Using Smoked Paprika Substitutes</span></h3> \n <ol>\n  <li>Utilize other types of paprika to get the paprika flavor without the smokiness. Try equal amounts of Hungarian, sweet, or hot paprika powder in your recipes instead of smoked paprika. These paprikas don’t have the smoky flavor, but at least you’ll get the pepper taste and red color of paprika.<sup id=\"_ref-8\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 8\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-8\">[8]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-8.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 8.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/71/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-8.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-8.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>This would probably be best for recipes that only call for small amounts of smoked paprika, in which the difference won’t be super noticeable.</li> \n    <li>If you’re making a recipe that relies heavily on smoked paprika for the seasoning, try a different alternative that recreates the smokiness of it.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Try chipotle powder for a very similar store-bought substitute. Store-bought chipotle powder is widely considered to be the best substitute for smoked paprika. Use the same amount of chipotle powder as the amount of smoked paprika that your recipe calls for.<sup id=\"_ref-9\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 9\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-9\">[9]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-9.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 9.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/7/7a/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-9.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-9.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Chipotle powder is made out of smoked, dried jalapeño peppers, which have a similar flavor profile to the smoked peppers used to make smoked paprika.</li> \n    <li>Some chipotle powders can be spicier than smoked paprika, depending on how hot the jalapeños used to make them were. If you don’t like the heat, reduce the amount of chipotle powder you use by 1/4 or so or just add it a little at a time to taste.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Use liquid smoke instead of smoked paprika to replicate the smokey flavor. Use half as much liquid smoke as you would smoked paprika in your recipe. Measure out liquid smoke in 1/2 the amount of the smoked paprika that your recipe calls for and pour it in. This will infuse a smoky flavor into the food to provide the essential component that smoked paprika contains.<sup id=\"_ref-10\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 10\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-10\">[10]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-10.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 10.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0f/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-10.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-10.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>For example, if your recipe calls for 1 tsp (2.3 g) of smoked paprika, use of liquid smoke instead.</li> \n    <li>You can add 1/2 tsp (1.65 g) of a different kind of paprika for each of liquid smoke to add some paprika flavor and color as well.</li> \n    <li>Liquid smoke is usually available in the spice aisle of your local supermarket, alongside BBQ seasoning mixes and similar things. Alternatively, you can order it online.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Mix 2 parts sweet paprika with 1 part cumin for a passable substitute. Combine sweet paprika and cumin in a 2-1 ratio in a small bowl and mix them together thoroughly. Add this mix to your recipe in the same amount as the smoked paprika that the recipe calls for.<sup id=\"_ref-11\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 11\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-11\">[11]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-11.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 11.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/0/0c/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-11.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-11.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>The sweet paprika will give you the color and flavor of paprika, while the cumin adds a bit of smokiness.</li> \n    <li>Cumin also naturally pairs well with the flavors in many dishes that call for smoked paprika, so it won’t harm your recipe at all.</li>\n   </ul></li> \n  <li>Choose cayenne, guajillo, or ancho pepper powders for smoky alternatives. These are 3 types of peppers that all have natural smoky, spicy flavors to certain degrees. Use these in recipes instead of smoked paprika in equal amounts or to taste.<sup id=\"_ref-12\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 12\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-12\">[12]</a></sup>\n   <div class=\"mwimg  largeimage  floatcenter \" style=\"max-width:728px\">\n    <a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Image:Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-12.jpg\" class=\"image\"><img alt=\"Make Smoked Paprika Step 12.jpg\" src=\"https://www.wikihow.com/images/thumb/3/30/Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-12.jpg/aid12099418-v4-728px-Make-Smoked-Paprika-Step-12.jpg\" decoding=\"async\" width=\"728\" height=\"546\" class=\"whcdn\" /></a>\n   </div> \n   <ul>\n    <li>Cayenne is the spiciest of these options, so use it if you want to add extra heat to your dishes.</li> \n    <li>You can also mix these into other types of paprika or into paprika combined with cumin to make your own kind of spice blend that is similar to smoked paprika.</li>\n   </ul></li>\n </ol> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6\" title=\"Edit section: Tips\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Tips\">Tips</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>Store-bought smoked paprika is made by smoking capsicum peppers for days on end. You can cheat to achieve similar results at home by using a smoker and a food dehydrator or an oven.<sup id=\"_ref-13\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 13\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-13\">[13]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>Smoked paprika is a key ingredient in many Spanish dishes and foods, such as paella, chorizo, and salami.<sup id=\"_ref-14\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 14\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-14\">[14]</a></sup></li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7\" title=\"Edit section: Warnings\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Warnings\">Warnings</span></h2> \n <ul>\n  <li>If you’re sensitive to spiciness, be careful what substitutes you use instead of smoked paprika. Other chili powders, such as cayenne or chipotle, are hotter than paprika, so you might want to add less or use a different substitute if you’re worried about the heat.<sup id=\"_ref-15\" class=\"reference\" aria-label=\"Link to Reference 15\"><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/Make-Smoked-Paprika#_note-15\">[15]</a></sup></li> \n  <li>Be careful when you’re cutting hot peppers if you choose to make homemade paprika out of chili peppers. Wear gloves to protect your hands and don’t touch your face or eyes.</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8\" title=\"Edit section: Things You’ll Need\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span id=\"Things-You’ll-Need\"></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Things-You.E2.80.99ll-Need\">Things You’ll Need</span></h2> \n <h3><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\" href=\"https://www.wikihow.com/index.php?title=Make-Smoked-Paprika&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9\" title=\"Edit section: Creating Your Own Smoked Paprika\">Edit</a><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">]</span></span><span class=\"mw-headline\" id=\"Creating-Your-Own-Smoked-Paprika_2\">Creating Your Own Smoked Paprika</span></h3> \n <ul>\n  <li>Red peppers</li> \n  <li>Kitchen towel or paper towels</li> \n  <li>Cutting board</li> \n  <li>Sharp knife</li> \n  <li>Gloves (optional)</li> \n  <li>Oak wood chips</li> \n  <li>Smoker</li> \n  <li>Dehydrator or oven</li> \n  <li>Dehydrator tray or baking tray</li> \n  <li>Spice or coffee grinder</li> \n  <li>Bowl</li> \n  <li>Fine mesh strainer</li> \n  <li>Sealable container</li>\n </ul> \n <h2><span class=\"mw-editsection\"><span class=\"mw-editsection-bracket\">[</span><a target=\"_blank\"
